Local News

Finance Ministry Announces Continued Collection of Income Tax; Banking and Monetary Industries Held Joint Meeting Yesterday; Resolved to Comply and Agreed on Various Collection Procedures; Various Freelance Professional Groups Held Discussions Yesterday

Following the Finance Ministry's announcement that it would continue collecting income taxes on securities deposits and other items from New Year's Day, the Banking and Monetary Industries Association held a joint meeting yesterday and resolved to comply. Various freelance professional groups held practical research discussions yesterday. Details are as follows:

Finance Ministry Announcement: Continued Collection

Finance Ministry Announcement No. 186 states: The various income taxes to be continued from January 1, year 26, are listed as follows: Category 1: Income from profit-making enterprises. A. Income from companies, firms, businesses, factories, or individuals with capital of 2,000 yuan or more. B. Income from joint government-business ventures. C. Income from temporary profit-making enterprises. Category 2: Income from salaries and remuneration. Income from salaries and remuneration of freelancers and other professionals. Category 3: Income from securities deposits. Income from company bonds, stocks, and deposit interest. For the above items, the tax rates, calculations, and payment procedures shall be handled in accordance with the Provisional Income Tax Regulations and their implementing rules. In addition to separate orders for handling, a public announcement is made for general knowledge. This announcement is made by Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Finance.

Banking and Monetary Industries: Joint Meeting

The Bankers Association held its 19th Executive Committee meeting at its Hong Kong Road location at 5:00 PM yesterday. The Monetary Industry Association was also invited to send representatives to jointly discuss the procedures for implementing income tax. Present were Chen Guangfu, Wu Yunzhai, Li Fusun, Wang Boyuan, Zhang Peishen, Hu Xi'an, Wu Weiru, Du Yuesheng, Song Ziliang (representing Zhang Zhuyu), Pan Jiufen, Qi Yunqing, and others from the Bankers Association Executive Committee; Pei Yunqing and Feng Yigui, representatives from the Monetary Industry Association; and Secretary-General Lin Kanghou in attendance. Chairman Chen Guangfu reported that the Ministry of Finance had decided to implement the first category of income from profit-making enterprises and the second category of income from salaries and remuneration on New Year's Day and requested a joint discussion on various collection procedures. The members expressed their opinions successively and reached an agreement on various collection procedures, resolving to comply with the Ministry's order and implement it as scheduled. Regarding the report of the previous subcommittee, it was also resolved that the two associations would submit contributions of their opinions to the Ministry. The meeting adjourned at 5:40 PM.

Banking Society: Research Report

A reporter from the New Voice Society learned yesterday of the Banking Society's second research report abstract on income tax. The section on deposits is as follows: (1) Interbank deposits should be tax-exempt. (Reason) The purpose of interbank deposits is to facilitate fund transfers between banks, which differs from the purpose of ordinary depositors seeking interest. (2) Interest on transactions between head offices and branches should be tax-exempt. (Reason) Banks provide services to society, and there are frequent fund transfers between head offices and branches. This is internal accounting, not ordinary business income. (3) The method for paying income tax on fixed deposits withdrawn in installments and installments paid out as a lump sum should be specified. (Reason) Both of these are settled semi-annually. If income tax is levied on the interest each time it is settled, the former will affect the originally scheduled amount for each installment, and the latter will affect the lump sum due in the future. A method should be devised to remedy this. (4) For various tax-exempt deposits, the bank should declare that it is not responsible for identifying them. (Reason) Article 2, Paragraph 3, Subparagraphs (Zi) (Yin) (Mao) of the regulations stipulate that interest income from funds deposited by government agencies and educational charities is exempt from income tax. However, it is difficult for banks to determine whether this type of deposit matches the actual situation. Depositors should be responsible for this themselves.

Freelance Groups: Hold Discussion

Freelance professional groups held a joint discussion at 3:00 PM yesterday at the Bankers Association on Hong Kong Road. Attendees included Xie Linfu, Jiang Wanping, He Yuanming, and more than ten other representatives from the Lawyers Association, Accountants Association, Chinese Institute of Engineers, Chinese Institute of Architects, National Medical Association, Shanghai Medical Association, Shanghai Chinese Medicine Association, and Chinese Medicine Society. They discussed the income tax issue for freelancers. The result was that each association would conduct further practical research, and representatives would be publicly nominated to go to Beijing to negotiate with the Ministry of Finance when necessary. The New Year's Day of the 26th year will arrive in the blink of an eye. In order to hold celebrations, the city's party headquarters specially followed the central government's regulations, formulated celebration methods, and scheduled a commemorative celebration at 10:00 AM on New Year's Day in the Great Hall of the City Chamber of Commerce, and notified all sectors to take a three-day holiday from New Year's Day and celebrate by hanging flags. The methods are recorded as follows: (1) Convene representatives from all sectors to hold the "Shanghai Municipal All Sectors Representatives Conference to Celebrate the 26th Anniversary of the Founding of the Republic of China." (2) Date: 10:00 AM on New Year's Day. (3) Venue: Great Hall of the City Chamber of Commerce. (4) The conference presidium will be composed of eight agencies and organizations: the Municipal Government, the Garrison Headquarters, the Municipal Farmers Association, the General Labor Union, the City Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Education Association, and the Municipal Women's Association. (5) Post a public notice in the newspaper for three days starting from the 30th of this month. (1) All organs, groups, schools, and residences in this city shall hang flags to celebrate. (2) All organs, groups, schools, and party departments at all levels shall send representatives to participate in the conference. (3) All sectors will take a three-day holiday from New Year's Day. (6) Send a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to send a band to the venue to play music. (7) Issue a letter to comrades and compatriots to celebrate the 26th anniversary of the founding of the Republic of China. (8) Send a letter to the Public Utilities Bureau, the Public Bus Management Office, the China Merchants Electric Tramway Company, and the Shanghai South and Zhabei Bus Companies, requiring all vehicles to hang flags to celebrate when driving on New Year's Day.

Food Transportation and Sales Bureau Officially Established Yesterday; Ceremony to be Held on New Year's Day

According to Shen Shi News Agency, the Ministry of Finance, in view of the fact that China's food supply is severely insufficient every year, in order to coordinate national food, adjust food production and sales, and prepare for a comprehensive plan, and seek methods of relief, specially drafted the Provisional Organization Regulations for the Food Transportation and Sales Bureau in February of the 24th year of the Republic of China, which was submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgation. Recently, considering that the bureau needs to be established earlier, it formally appointed Zheng Baozhao, former Deputy Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, as the Director of the Food Transportation and Sales Bureau, and Tang Guozhen as the Deputy Director, to actively carry out preparations.

Director Takes Office

After being appointed, Zheng and Tang went to Beijing to meet with Minister Kong for instructions and decided to set up the General Bureau in Shanghai, finding a house at No. 534 Xiaoshadu Road in West Shanghai as the bureau's address. Everything was completed on the 25th, and it was officially established yesterday. Zheng Baozhao and Tang Guozhen, the Director and Deputy Director, arrived at the bureau on the same day and took office. After convening all staff at 9:00 AM and giving instructions, they began to work and decided to officially hold an establishment ceremony on New Year's Day, inviting the Ministry of Finance to send personnel for guidance.

Staff List

As for the bureau's organization, branch bureaus will be established under the General Bureau. The areas where the branch bureaus will be established will depend on the convenience of food production, sales, and the exercise of their functions. Internally, there are four sections, and domestic food scholars and technicians are hired as specialists. Yesterday, the list of senior staff of the Shanghai General Bureau was announced: Secretary Bian Hanjie, Section Chief Hong Ruitao, Section Chief Shen Guojin, Specialist Sun Yue, Song Jianxun, Fang Peishou, etc. Currently, two sections have been established.

China National Aviation Corporation; Announces Business Status; From October to the End of October This Year

China National Aviation Corporation announced its business status yesterday: From January to the end of October this year, it flew a total of 2,018,064 kilometers, carrying 14,817 passengers and 60,541 kilograms of mail. Last year, it flew a total of 1,906,452 kilometers, carrying 11,004 passengers and 74,045 kilograms of mail. The average increase reached one-third. When the company was first established in 1929, it flew only 93,369 kilometers, carried 350 passengers, and 3,932 kilograms of mail. Business development can be clearly understood from the figures.

Xiang River Floods; Navigation is Fully Open

Changsha, Hunan, had an early water recession this year. At its shallowest point, the Xiang River had only one foot of water, causing all ships to stop and be unable to pass, only reaching Yuezhou. Goods going to Changsha were mostly accumulated in Hankou and Yuezhou ports. Although there were civilian boats transshipping, the capacity was too small, causing extreme stagnation. The Xiang gang was deeply anxious because the end of the year was approaching. Changsha sent a telegram yesterday reporting that the Xiang River's water level had risen sharply in recent days due to heavy rainfall, increasing to seven feet six inches, and navigation was fully open. Shallow-water ships can travel smoothly. At the request of various guest gangs, all shipping companies have dispatched large barges to Yuezhou to load and enter Hunan with all the goods that are stockpiled there.

Large Batch of Huainan Coal; To Be Shipped to Shanghai Soon; River Water Rises Greatly, Shipping is Smooth

Due to the large drop in the Yangtze River's water level, larger and deeper merchant ships could not load at Yuxikou. Now that the Yangtze River has risen greatly, Wuhu has eighteen feet of water, and ocean-going ships can now sail. This city received reliable information yesterday that six ocean-going ships have arrived at Yuxikou to transport a large amount of coal to Shanghai and are being loaded. Within a few days, a large batch of Huainan coal can be loaded and transported to Shanghai to meet the needs of society.

Reorganization of the Municipal Public Security Bureau; Name Changed to Police Bureau; Three-Tier System Changed to Two-Tier System

Regarding the issue of reforming the national police system, the Ministry of the Interior has drafted a plan and sent it to the provincial and municipal governments, requiring them to reorganize according to the new plan. According to sources from the Municipal Public Security Authority, this city will also implement reorganization. The name of the Public Security Bureau will be changed to the Police Bureau. At the same time, the current three-tier system will be changed to a two-tier system, that is, the existing police stations will be abolished, and branch bureaus will be established directly under the General Bureau to facilitate command. In the future, branch bureaus will be increased as appropriate, and police forces will also be appropriately strengthened. However, whether the Security Corps will be transferred to the jurisdiction of the police authorities is still under consideration. Therefore, the reorganization of the police administration in this city will be difficult to realize on New Year's Day and will probably occur after January or February.

Bankers Association Holds Member Meeting Yesterday; Chairman Chen Guangfu Reports on Association Affairs This Year; Approves This Year's Final Accounts and Next Year's Budget

The Shanghai Bankers Association held its 10th Member Meeting at its Hong Kong Road headquarters at 4:00 PM yesterday, reporting on the handling of association affairs this year and approving the final accounts for this year and the budget for the first half of the 26th year. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Members

A total of 109 representatives from 43 member banks, including Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Dalu Bank, Kenye Bank, Silk Industry Bank, Si Ming Bank, Jin Cheng Bank, Xinhua Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Real Estate Bank, China Industrial Bank, China National Products Bank, Tonghe Bank, Tongshang Bank, Zhonghui Bank, Quangong Bank, Women's Bank, and others, including Chen Guangfu, Sun Jingxi, Yao Yinpeng, Qin Runqing, Du Yuesheng, Lu Zidong, Wang Boyuan, Fu Xiao'an, Jing Runshi, Wu Yunzhai, Liu Pinsan, Tang Shoumin, Wang Zhixin, Qi Yunqing, Wu Weiru, Xu Xinliu, Hu Bijang, Ye Zhuotang, Wang Shaoxian, Zhu Miaosheng, Li Fusun, Hu Xi'an, Zhang Peishen, Pan Jiufen, Zhang Zhuyu, Bei Songsun, Chen Mutang, Zhang Shulin, and Liu Hongyuan, were present. Secretary-General Lin Kanghou and Recorder Gu Cheng'an were in attendance.

Chairman's Report

After performing the rituals, Chairman Chen Guangfu reported on the association's affairs since the 11th session: "Looking back, this association was established five years ago, in the 20th year of the Republic of China, succeeding the former Shanghai Bankers Association. Initially, only 28 banks joined, less than three-eighths of the city's banks. The number of member representatives was only over 140. Over the years, there have been additions, and recently there have been 43 members, and the number of representatives has increased to over 170. The foundation is gradually solid, and the responsibilities are heavier. This association handles association affairs with practicality as the main principle. In the past few years, all measures have been based on the country's economic revival policy and the refreshing of the industry's business plan. In these difficult times, there is not much to mention, but the original intention of maintaining the financial bulwark has always been consistent and is well understood by the colleagues present. This year, Chairman Chen Guangfu went abroad for public affairs and returned after half a year. Permanent Committee Member Wu Yunzhai served as acting chairman, handling everything according to the established rules. After the chairman returned to work in early November, a total of eight executive committee meetings, two group meetings, and one joint meeting of the banking and monetary industries were convened during this six-month period. In addition to routine matters that do not need to be repeated, the more important cases handled include the following: Regarding the entry and exit of members, such as the Jiangzhe Bank merging with the Zhonghui Bank for business, a letter was sent requesting the cancellation of membership. The Guangdong Bank has now announced its resumption of business and has also sent a letter requesting to rejoin the list of member banks. The Executive Committee has approved this year and included it in today's agenda, pending ratification by the General Assembly. As for the income tax issue, it was originally scheduled to be implemented in October this year, but the Ministry of Finance approved a postponement of implementation after this association presented it. At the same time, a subcommittee was organized to revise the internal procedures in detail. As this case is a new policy for the 26th year, I will only mention the beginning and will make a systematic report at the next regular meeting. As for the two donations for buying machines to celebrate birthdays and the one-day sports, all banks in this association also strongly supported them, totaling approximately 20,000 yuan or more. There are also opinions on abolishing the current bank guarantee system and unifying the rules for foreign exchange business, which are related to the industry's practical affairs and are being planned for implementation. This can be reported in advance. In addition to publishing a compilation of circulars, this association will further plan to compile books such as association affairs compendiums, which will not only provide convenience for colleagues to investigate at any time, but also provide a consistent description of this association's work. Colleagues are burdened with heavy responsibilities, and there is a deep fear of failure. It is hoped that those colleagues in the city who have not joined the association will help each other in the same boat and come to join successively. Then, the strength will be thick, and the effect will be great. Regarding the promotion of association affairs and the reform of the industry's advantages and disadvantages, we rely more on the feelings of each member, who will give assistance from time to time. Hopefully, we can gather our thoughts and benefit not only the future of this association, which can be expected to progress day by day, but also those in the association. This is not a small matter. On the occasion of convening the annual regular meeting, I have written a few words to record the general outline of the association's affairs in the past six months."

Passing Various Cases

After the chairman's report, the following cases were discussed: (1) The Jiangzhe Commercial Savings Bank's letter requesting to withdraw from the association was passed. (2) The Guangdong Bank's letter requesting to be relisted as a member bank of this association was passed. (3) The Zhejiang Industrial, China Industrial, Zhongfu, Silk Industry, and Zhonghui Banks' letters requesting to replace member representatives were passed. (4) The final accounts for the next session of this association were passed. (5) The budget for the first half of the 26th year was passed. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Cui Tongyue's Remains Moved to the Central Funeral Home Yesterday; Mayor Wu and Others Attended the Memorial Service; Funeral Scheduled for the 3rd of Next Month

According to the "Shen Shi News," the passing of the revolutionary pioneer Cui Tongyue (Min) the day before yesterday morning has caused great sorrow among all parties who learned of the news. His remains have now been moved to the Central Funeral Home, and the funeral is scheduled for the 3rd of next month. The funeral committee has reported the death to the Central Party Headquarters and President Sun. The reporter of "Shen Shi News" is now reporting on the various circumstances as follows:

Many Mourners

Mr. Cui's remains were moved to the Central Funeral Home yesterday morning. Those who went to pay their respects included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director of the Education Bureau Pan Gongzhan, Central Committee members Xie Chi and Yang Shukan, as well as Mr. Cui's friends Zai Yucheng, Zheng Ziliang, Li Yiqin, Tang Haian, Li Dachao, Cen Xiquan, Zhou Xunyu, Zhuo Wuchu, Gao Fengchi, and many others.

Mr. Cui's Will

"I am old and my health has always been weak. It is a gift from heaven that I have lived to be seventy years old. I regret that I cannot die at the same time with other old comrades who do not covet merit or speak of reward. While in bed, I suddenly heard that Chairman Chiang Kai-shek was in distress in Xi'an, which caused me to lose sleep for several nights. Now he has escaped danger and returned to Nanjing, just like when President Sun Yat-sen was in distress at the London Embassy. This is the effect of prayer. However, everything in China goes according to heaven. If we can strive to fight, we will surely exist forever in the world. I hope that all people will unite and overcome this difficulty, so as to achieve the goal of national freedom and liberation in China. Regarding the affairs of establishing the Jianru Library and the Youlie Memorial Hall in the Canghai School, I hope that all colleagues will do their best to carry them out. The Qinian Association has been operating miserably for five years, and has already received two mu of land donated by the founder of the Longhua Orphanage to build a nursing home. It is planned to build a small house on the remaining land in the back so that my wife, Ms. Jiang, can take care of the affairs of the nursing home. The Overseas Chinese Federation and various organizations should cooperate to seek welfare for overseas Chinese and compatriots. My lifelong aspirations and experiences are all described in detail in the two books, 'Canghai's Life' and 'Collection of Poems'. Now that the country is in serious trouble, the funeral should be frugal and do not waste the time and money of relatives, friends, and comrades." Cui Tongyue's will, 25, 12, 27, afternoon. Recorded by Xie Zitian, Cen Xiquan, Shen Zuoliang, Jiang Min, Cui Aiying, Cui Boyi, Lai Yinlin, Wei Jianwei.

Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Association Reorganized; First Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday

The preparatory committee for reorganizing the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Association into the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Trade Association Federation held its first preparatory meeting yesterday afternoon. More than 20 representatives from silk weaving industries in Shanghai, Suzhou, Hangzhou, Huzhou, and Danyang attended the meeting. Wang Jiean was elected as chairman. The results of the discussion were: (1) The federation will be based on each trade association as a unit, and each association should send three representatives to attend. The resumes of the representatives should be sent to the meeting by letter for filing. (2) If the number of representatives sent by local associations is less than three, they should immediately send enough representatives to make up the number. (3) All application procedures to be handled by the federation shall be fully handled by the chairman. (4) The draft charter shall be decided by the chairman after consulting with the party and government agencies first. (5) Letters shall be sent to silk industry associations in various places that have not yet joined, asking them to join the federation in order to seek welfare through unity, and to send representatives and resumes by letter. (6) Except for important matters concerning the whole body, which must be discussed at a general meeting of all representatives, other matters shall be solicited in writing to avoid representatives traveling back and forth.

Suiyuan Relief Association Cables the Jishi Society for Relief; Requests Relief for the War Zone Disaster

The Chinese Jishi Society recently received a telegram from the Suiyuan Provincial Relief Association, which stated: "Upon investigation, the people in the war zones in eastern and northern Suiyuan, along Xinghe, Taolin, Jining, Wuchuan, and other counties, suffered disasters in a total of forty or fifty villages and towns. The most serious ones, such as Honggeertu, Xinaobao, Sanyanjing, and Dajiangou, were either attacked and looted, or bombed by airplanes, heavy artillery, poison gas, tanks, and other sharp weapons. The number of villagers poisoned and killed is countless. The destruction of all buildings and the looting of grain and property, in some cases the entire village was emptied. The severity of the disaster is unprecedented. Now, refugees in various places are displaced, crying for food and shivering in the ice and snow, which is extremely miserable. If no measures are taken to provide relief, they will inevitably fill the ditches. Our association has witnessed the disaster and is extremely saddened. In addition to raising relief funds with all the strength of the province, we should urgently appeal to the nobles, so that the benevolence and generosity will be continuously supplied, so that the remaining victims can be fully alive. We earnestly hope that you will be generous and give relief. We are extremely hopeful. A special telegram is sent to you." The association has already forwarded the telegram to the Shanghai United Relief Association of Charitable Organizations, requesting relief. It is also hoped that charitable comrades at home and abroad will generously donate to save these victims from their unfounded disaster.

Announcement from the Money Trade Association on Reforming Check Styles

In addition to implementing the national calendar's New Year's Eve accounting, the Shanghai Money Trade Association has decided to use new-style accounting starting next year. It has also scheduled a meeting of members' representatives at 9:00 a.m. today to decide on interest rates, etc. Yesterday, it issued a special notice to member money houses regarding the reform of check styles: "The undersigned respectfully reports that, as approved by the proposal of the temporary executive committee on the 26th of this month, most of the checks used by the money houses do not have the words 'or bearer' printed on them. Hereafter, please add the words 'or bearer' to the checks used by the money houses to comply with the check format. Also, the money houses have not had seals for distribution to various money houses and banks. Now, for the sake of facilitating verification, it is resolved that each money house must print a seal with the signature and seal of the manager, assistant manager, and chief accountant, and distribute it to various money houses and banks for verification." This is recorded in the minutes and is hereby notified for your information and compliance. Respectfully addressed to all member money houses for your attention.

Buddhist Organizations to Cast Jiuhua Netherworld Bell; Furnace to be Opened and Bell Cast on the Mountain Today

Six organizations, including the Chinese Buddhist Association of Shanghai, jointly initiated the fundraising to build a large bronze bell weighing 20,000 catties, to be placed on the top of Jiuhua Mountain in Anhui, to solemnize the Bodhimanda of Ksitigarbha Bodhisattva and embellish the scenery. It has been decided to open the furnace and cast the bell today (i.e., the birthday of Amitabha Buddha in the Buddhist calendar) at the old site of Laodongya Temple on Jiuhua Mountain. The details have been reported in this newspaper. It is learned that the representatives sent by the Buddhist Lay Forest and others to participate in the casting ceremony have sent a telegram reporting the preparation of the bell casting project as follows: More than one hundred copper smelting pots and stoves are planned to be used, and have been prepared, so that by the deadline, all 20,000 catties of copper material can be placed in the pots and burned and melted. When it becomes liquid, hundreds of small workers will be ordered to draw from the pots separately and transfer it to a very large iron pot prepared separately, and then fire it to stir evenly. The mud-shaped bell mold is located below the large pot, and then it is connected with an iron pipe. As soon as the mechanism is activated, the huge amount of copper liquid in the pot will be poured into the mold in a moment. After the copper cools down, the mold shell is removed, and the bell is completed. It is also said that all plans are in place and the smelting and casting will be carried out on schedule. In addition, the Huaguang Radio Station will broadcast the holy name of Namo Ksitigarbha Bodhisattva all day today to celebrate the completion of the bell.

Lawyer Wang Peiyuan Removed from the Register of Lawyers

Lawyer Wang Peiyuan, while practicing law in Shanghai in August 24 of the Republic of China, stole money and gold jewelry from the luggage deposited by the Suzhou women Liu Yin and Liu Yuee, mother and daughter. After the case was discovered, Liu Yin and her daughter sued him at the Prosecutor's Office of the Wuxian Local Court. After investigation, he was sentenced to imprisonment. At that time, because he disagreed with the verdict, he appealed to the Jiangsu Higher Court and was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and five years of deprivation of civil rights. Although his sentence has been completed and he has been released from prison, the Jiangsu Higher Court Lawyers' Disciplinary Committee has decided to remove him from the register and revoke his lawyer's license. The Jiangsu Higher Court has now ordered the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office to order the Shanghai Lawyers' Association to inquire about Wang Peiyuan's residence and to immediately submit the lawyer's license for revocation. The main text of the resolution of the Lawyers' Disciplinary Committee is excerpted as follows: Lawyer Wang Peiyuan, 39 years old, (main text) removal from the register, (facts) Wang Peiyuan practiced law in the Shanghai Lawyers' Association. In August 24 of the Republic of China, because he was handling the separation of Liu Yuee, a woman living in Suzhou, from her mother Liu Yin, he took the opportunity to collude with his sister Wang Lixia and continuously stole the silver, gold, and jewelry in the boxes deposited by Liu Yin and her daughter. After Liu Yin and her daughter discovered it, they sued him to the Wuxian Local Court, which sentenced Yu Peiyuan to imprisonment. Because he disagreed, he appealed, and the Jiangsu Higher Court, on February 11 of this year, changed the sentence to one year of imprisonment and five years of deprivation of civil rights in accordance with Article 28, Article 56, and Article 320, Paragraph 1, Article 37, Section 2 of the Criminal Law. The chief prosecutor of the Jiangsu Higher Court then filed a disciplinary suit with the association in his official capacity (reasons) According to Article 4 of the Lawyers' Regulations, those who have one of the following situations shall not be allowed to serve as lawyers. Section 2 of the same article states that those who have been sentenced to detention or imprisonment of five years or more shall not be allowed to serve as lawyers. Wang Peiyuan, the lawyer who was charged in this case, (the case is the same as before, omitted) In accordance with the foregoing provisions, he should be removed from the register. In accordance with Article 37, Section 3 of the Lawyers' Regulations, the resolution is as stated in the main text, and so on.

Shen Lijuan Accuses Ni Lusheng of Bigamy

Ni Lusheng, from Liuzhao Bay, Nanhui, Pudong, was formerly an employee of a grain store in Shanghai. Shen Lijuan, a 22-year-old woman from Suzhou living at 583 Yongxing Road, Zhabei, was quite beautiful. Ni was captivated and, through various means, married her as his wife on October 16th of the 21st year of the Republic [1932]. Their relationship was initially good. However, Ni recently opened a grain store in his hometown, so he took Shen Lijuan back with him. It turned out that Ni not only had a wife but also children. Initially, Ni claimed his wife was his sister-in-law, but after a few days, the truth of the children calling him "father" and his wife "mother" was revealed. At the same time, the neighbors looked at Lijuan and whispered "concubine." Lijuan was furious and returned to Shanghai in anger. She hired lawyer Xu Jianjie to file a lawsuit in the local court, accusing Ni Lusheng of fraudulent marriage and bigamy, and requesting punishment under Article 237 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday, Judge Wu Xiangzu held a court session, but because the defendant did not appear, the hearing was adjourned to a later date.

Firecracker Explosion: Right Hand Blown Off

Liu Asi, a 45-year-old man from Taixing, residing at 99 Tiandeng Lane, Xundao Street, Nanshi, was engaged in manufacturing and selling firecrackers. He employed several female workers to assist in the work. Dock Gangsters: Extortion Attempt Leads to Feces Attack

The Sanbei Company's Fengpu Wheel was docked at the Hongsheng Wharf of Laiyi Ferry in Pudong at 4:00 AM on the 19th of this month when a fire broke out in the aft hold, destroying a large quantity of lumber, machinery, fireworks, tobacco leaves, grains, and other items. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. The remaining burned tobacco leaves were auctioned by Ruihe Foreign Firm, with 120 pieces purchased by Yu Xin Tobacco Company of the French Concession for 20 yuan each. Yu Luxin, the owner of the company from Shandong, chartered a boat and hired coolies to transport the tobacco leaves onto the boat. Yesterday morning, while they were working, a large group of dock gangsters demanded "regulations money," claiming that another tobacco factory had purchased 170 pieces and had paid 130 yuan in "tips." Yu argued that these tobacco leaves were not smuggled goods and there was no need for "expenses," so he telephoned the Pudong Sub-Bureau to request protection. The bureau dispatched a senior officer to maintain order. The gangsters, unable to extort money, dispersed. At noon, Yu went to Hongyun Restaurant in Laiyi Ferry for lunch and then returned to the dock with a police officer to watch over the goods. As they walked to the west of Yulong Bank on Dongchang Road, a group of thugs suddenly emerged, holding three cigarette boxes filled with excrement, and dumped them on Yu's head. The thugs, seeing their goal achieved, fled. Yu was covered in excrement from head to toe, filled with rage, and reported the incident to the Sub-Bureau, which dispatched officers to arrest Cen Wenfa from Gaoyou and Gu Xiangfu from Chongming, two of the perpetrators. Cen confessed that the day before, Yu had asked him to hire two boats for 27 yuan, but today he refused to pay. He said that many gangsters demanded "expenses" and told him to throw feces. Gu denied any involvement. The Sub-Bureau Chief ordered them to be sent to the General Bureau for interrogation and ordered the continued pursuit of the other gangsters for severe punishment.

Theft of Telephone Lines: Culprits Sentenced by Garrison Headquarters

Zhou Xiang and Two Others Sentenced to Five Years Imprisonment; Receiving Stolen Goods Crime: Fine Imposed

The theft of electric and telephone wires has occurred frequently in the city. The Ministry of Communications has offered rewards for the capture of the perpetrators, and the Headquarters has issued a strict prohibition order. However, there are still unscrupulous individuals who, disregarding the law, seize the opportunity to steal. Zhou Xiang from Zhuji, Yu Caoqiu (also known as Yu Xianzhang), and Li Ming from Hangzhou repeatedly stole electric wires in the Zhabei Bayu Bridge, Hongkou Huade Road, and near the Yangsi Bridge Railway Station in Pudong, as well as in Liuli Bridge in Pudong, and sold them to copper and tin shops for money. In one instance, the theft near the Yangsi Bridge Railway Station was discovered by Li Guisheng, an investigator from the Tangqiao Police Station of the Public Security Bureau, who apprehended Zhou Xiang. Zhou Xiang then confessed about Yu Caoqiu, and Yu Caoqiu confessed about Li Ming. The City Public Security Bureau arrested them all. Li Ming also revealed that the place where the stolen goods were sold was Guangli Copper and Tin Shop. The shop assistant, Lu Yongnian from Huzhou, was arrested along with a bundle of stolen telephone wires and sent to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters. After a detailed interrogation by the Military Law Office, Yu Caoqiu, Zhou Xiang, and Li Ming confessed to stealing electric wires and selling them for profit. Lu Yongnian also confessed to receiving stolen goods. Therefore, they were sentenced according to the law. Zhou Xiang, Yu Caoqiu (also known as Yu Xianzhang), and Li Ming were each sentenced to five years of imprisonment for jointly and continuously disrupting telephone communications, and each was deprived of their civil rights for five years. Lu Yongnian was fined for receiving stolen goods to show strict punishment.

Shanghai County Government Abolishes the "Kunye" System, Assigning Responsibility to Baojia Chiefs

Since the implementation of the land value tax in Shanghai County, property owners in various districts have been actively paying at the hub. The distribution of grain vouchers and minor tax matters in each district were handled by the "kunye" (捆業) of each "tu" (圖). Since the implementation of land value tax registration, the boundaries of each "tu" have been completely abolished. Land value tax notices are now distributed by the township chiefs. The previous "kunye" system has been explicitly abolished by the county government. From now on, the collection of land value taxes will be the responsibility of the township Baojia chiefs.

Shanghai Municipal Council Public Information Office Closes: Report Submitted by Qian Bohan, Head of Chinese Information

As the Municipal Council's Public Information Office is about to close, it is currently in the process of finalizing matters. Recently, Chairman Arnold and Director-General Felippu sent letters to the Public Information Office, thanking the Chinese, English, and Japanese directors for their past service. It is also reported that Qian Bohan, the head of Chinese Information, has submitted the 1936 work report to the Director-General's Office. This report is also the final report of the Public Information Office in the five years since its establishment. The following is a summary of the main points: A total of more than 440 Chinese information items were issued this year. More than 160 Chinese newspaper reviews and records were translated into English for reference by the board and relevant departments. The Chinese information issued by the Public Information Office, due to its close relationship with various Chinese newspapers and news agencies, was readily published, benefiting the authorities greatly. For example, the effective publicity of sanitation matters has been of great benefit to both the authorities and the citizens. As for the comments on bureau affairs in Chinese newspapers, although the Chinese citizens are gradually paying more attention to the bureau's administration, the opinions published in newspapers still lack a consistent policy and only discuss individual accidental events in a passive manner. Active and systematic contributions are still rare. As for the most reported events in Chinese newspapers this year, the rickshaw issue and the shantytown issue occupied a very prominent position. Other issues such as cross-border road construction and factory inspection were also frequently reported. However, major issues with news value, such as disputes caused by election errors, and the financial situation and austerity issues related to the interests of all citizens, were significantly less reported and criticized than in foreign newspapers. Other events that could be pursued, such as the telephone issue, were still being debated at the beginning of the year. In the summer, the Police Department's ban on patriotic dramas being performed in the concession also caused fierce criticism for a time.

Indian Police Officer to Be Hanged for Murder: Rope Breaks, Neck Not Broken; Law Seems to Indicate No Re-execution; Possible Pardon or Commutation; Indian Officer Not Dead But Suffers Concussion

The Greater Shanghai Evening Post reports that Indian police officer Atma Singh, who was sentenced to be hanged for killing Indian police officer Bawa Singh of the Putuo Road Police Station on October 19th, was to be executed at the Ward Road Prison at 7:00 AM this morning (29th). Unexpectedly, the executioner placed the noose around the convict's neck, pulled him up to the gallows, raised him to nine or ten feet, and the rope suddenly broke in the middle. The convict fell to the ground, but his neck was not broken. The attending officials were all horrified. This is rare in the history of executing criminals in Shanghai and the world. It is said that the execution rope had been tested last night and was very strong. It is unknown why it broke this morning. British Consul General to Shanghai, Sir Brenan, telegraphed British Ambassador to Peiping, Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, upon hearing the news. He also plans to go to Ward Road Prison tomorrow morning to investigate the truth. The convict did not die after falling to the ground, but suffered a concussion. He is now lying in the police station hospital. His final fate is currently uncertain. Many believe that a person who has been hanged should not be hanged again according to the law. In the past, convicts who were executed but did not die were often granted leniency. Sir Brenan is currently awaiting instructions from the British Ambassador on how to deal with the person, whether to grant him a pardon or a commutation. It is heard that the convict suffered a severe concussion, which may lead to his death. Ward Road prison officials are currently tight-lipped about the matter. When asked about the convict's condition, they replied that they did not know and suggested inquiring at the British Consulate. Reuters Peiping, 29th, reports that British Ambassador Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen has decided to commute the death sentence of Indian Atma Singh, the convict who was not killed when the rope broke during his execution in Shanghai this morning. Although the Ambassador's decision has not yet been announced, it is expected that the convict will have his sentence commuted to life imprisonment.

Briton Knox Attacked: Hoodlums Ambush on Ou Jia Road: Badly Injured by Acid

A Briton, Knox, (transliteration), a foreman at the Shanghai Water Company on Yangshupu Road, residing at 2 Mcgarry Road, Ti Si Wei Road, finished work yesterday afternoon and hired a rickshaw with the Shanghai City license plate number 1544 to return home. While passing the entrance of Lane 917 on Ou Jia Road, a thug, about 30 years old, suddenly jumped out of the opposite Zhe Xing Lane, stopped the rickshaw, and splashed nitric acid he was carrying on Knox's head. Smallpox Rampant: Vaccination Advised: Discussion with Director Li of the Health Bureau

Li Ting'an, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, is paying particular attention to the recent smallpox epidemic. He said that smallpox is an acute infectious disease caused by direct contact with patients or infection with their secretions. Children are particularly vulnerable, with a mortality rate of about 20%, which is frightening to mention. Few smallpox cases were found in Shanghai in October and November, one in October and two in November. However, it has been particularly rampant this month. According to statistics from the Shanghai Municipal Infectious Disease Hospital, it has admitted as many as 33 patients. This is due to the large population of Shanghai and the constant movement of people. The prevention method is early vaccination with cowpox. Both children and adults should be vaccinated. The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau's health stations in Hunan, Hubei, Jiangwan, Wusong, Gaoqiao, and other districts, as well as the Municipal Infectious Disease Hospital and the Municipal Hunan Hospital (formerly Shanghai Hospital), can all provide free vaccinations. To facilitate the public, 22 institutions, including Southeast Hospital, Tongde Hospital, Xin Puyu Hall, Sino-German Hospital, Pingmin Free Clinic, Shanghai Epidemic Hospital, Women and Children's Hospital, Emergency Epidemic Hospital, Nanyang Hospital, Huxi Commune, Waterside Pavilion Clinic, Pudong Hospital, Municipal Public Education Center, Children's Free Clinic, Taizhou Hospital, Pushan Hospital, Labor Hospital, Lianyi Western Hospital, Red Cross Hospital, and Second and Third Hospitals, and Hunan People's Maternity Hospital, have been designated as vaccination distribution points. Opportunities are available everywhere, so please do not miss them. If there are groups of 30 or more people, you can send a letter directly to the Municipal Health Bureau, and they will send personnel to vaccinate.

Counterfeit Coins: Organization Cracked: Models Seized: Several Arrested

Shao Jingfan, a Chinese detective of the Jiaxing Road Police Station, along with detective Yang Xinzheng and officer Chen Jinsheng, learned that Zhang Jinrong, the owner of the Hexing Printing House at 10 Lane 778, Peng Road, was involved in counterfeiting Farmers Bank 20-cent coins. They secretly raided the place at 8:40 PM the day before yesterday. While passing near North Jiangxi Road on Haining Road, they arrested a suspect, Zhang Jingkang from Anhui, and found a copper model of the reverse side of a Farmers Bank 20-cent coin, already mounted on wood. Detective Shao remained calm and went directly to the organization, where they arrested Yang Ganxiang from Pinghu, Zhu Fengtang from Haimen, Xu Fugao from Danyang, Yang Shaokang from Yunnan, apprentices Shen Jusheng from Wuxi, Qiang Baishun, Chen Xiangwen from Zhapu, and others. However, no other evidence was found. The owner, Zhang Jinrong, is on the run. They were all taken to the police station for detention and then sent to the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer Zhang Shizhu explained the case and requested an extension. A copper model was presented for inspection. Sun Derong, a representative of the Farmers Bank, testified that the model was of the third type of 20-cent coin, and that counterfeit coins had previously been found circulating in the market and had been destroyed. Zhang Jingkang, when questioned, said that he was a runner in the Hexing Printing House and that a friend, Qiu Wenxiang, had contacted him beforehand. The model was made by the owner, Zhang Jinrong. He made evasive replies. Yang Ganxiang said that the matter was done by Zhang Jingkang and the owner, that the model for the front side had not been made, and that he was not a shareholder. Xu Fugao said that he was a carpenter at the shop and knew nothing about it. Zhu Fengtang said that Zhang Jinrong had asked him to photograph the reverse side model presented in court and that the front side was not photographed. Yang Shaokang and the apprentices Shen Jusheng, Qiang Baishun, and Chen Xiangwen all claimed that they knew nothing about the matter. Judge Zhong Qing ordered all defendants to be remanded in custody for further review.

Social Affairs Bureau Order: Strictly Prohibit Depressing the Price of Subsidiary Currency; Stop Exchange Shops from Taking Advantage of the Year-End Period and Manipulating Exchange Rates Arbitrarily, Disregarding Regulations.

The Shanghai Money Trade Association issued a public notice in the market yesterday stating: "Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's Order No. 7802, which states: 'Based on reports from citizens, it is found that the Ministry of Finance's currency reform, which stipulates the value of silver dollars, truly benefits the people and prevents merchants from manipulating prices, has been clearly promulgated. However, recently, various exchange shops in the city have disregarded regulations, vigorously implementing their old methods. Every year-end approaches, they depress the price of silver dollars, with fluctuations of even twenty or thirty coins. At a time when people's livelihoods are difficult, these unscrupulous merchants are so inhumane and violate the promulgated orders. If they are not strictly stopped, they will become even more unscrupulous in the future.' Based on this, it is found that recently the exchange rate of national currency has suddenly fallen, and the exchange rates of copper coins, subsidiary currency, and small silver coins are not in accordance with regulations. The various exchange shops are suspected of manipulation. In addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued to the Association to investigate and stop this, and report back for verification. Furthermore, every year before the year-end settlement period in the city, the price of silver dollars is bound to fall, affecting citizens, which is no small matter. Since the currency reform, exchange rates have been stable, and the aforementioned situation should not occur again. As the year-end approaches, methods should be devised in advance to prevent this. The Association is hereby ordered to comply with this order and report back as necessary.' Having received this, it is found that our Association's members have never engaged in exchange business. In addition to submitting a reply, this notice is hereby issued."

Secretary of the "Blood Soul Exterminate Traitors" Group, Wang Zixiang, Questioned Yesterday; Police Present a Letter; Wang Has Admitted to Writing It.

Wang Zixiang, the secretary of the "Blood Soul Exterminate Traitors" Group, was apprehended by the Hangzhou Municipal Public Security Bureau and then escorted to Shanghai by Lang Jin'an, a Chinese detective from the Shanghai Old Zha Police Station, to be interrogated and detained by the Special First Court. This has already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide continued the trial in the first criminal court. In the winter of the 21st year of the Republic of China (1932), when the police apprehended Pan Hongsheng and others in connection with the bombing case and sent them to the court for trial, the chief officer of the Public Works Department received a letter on December 18 of that year, purportedly from the "Blood Soul Exterminate Traitors" Group, stating that Pan and others committed the crime out of patriotism and requesting favorable treatment. It also stated that only British and Japanese goods were prevalent in Shanghai and that banning Japanese goods would greatly benefit British goods. The handwriting of the letter was consistent with Wang's written confession and other letters, which proved that Wang was indeed a member of the "Blood Soul Exterminate Traitors" Group and should be punished according to law. When questioned, Wang Zixiang claimed that the letter was drafted by Wang Tiemin, who then ordered him to write it, claiming that it was for public organizations to rescue patriotic heroes, so he wrote it on their behalf. Lending Money at Usurious Rates and Committing Assault

Zhu Hongchen, a peddler from Zhenjiang, residing at No. 1, Sanjia Village, Pudong, makes a living by selling olives. This summer, due to financial difficulties and a lack of capital, he asked Zhong Detai (from Xinghua) to act as a guarantor and borrowed two silver dollars from Meng Shiguang, a Gaoyou native who specializes in lending money at usurious rates. He had to pay eight copper coins per day in interest (commonly known as "rubber ball money"). The interest would only stop once the principal of two silver dollars was repaid. However, business was poor, resulting in an accumulation of 480 copper coins in interest owed. Around 9 pm the night before, Meng demanded the interest from Zhu but was unable to obtain it, so he dragged Zhu out and beat him severely, causing serious injuries. The police arrived and took Meng to the station. Due to the case involving usurious lending and assault, he was transferred to the Public Security Bureau yesterday for investigation.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 315th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Convertible Notes states: "In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the number of convertible notes issued by this bank and the reserve fund. On December 26, 1936, the 315th inspection was conducted at the issuing bureau of this bank. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 32,559,2469 silver dollars, including 28,614,0952 silver dollar notes and 3,945,1517 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of the convertible note reserve fund is 32,559,2469 silver dollars, including 21,223,8769 silver dollars in cash. This cash reserve includes 99,626,169.48 silver dollars stored in the issuing headquarters, branches, and sub-branches of this bank, and 11,261,2599.52 silver dollars stored with other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 11,335,3700 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 400,9630.07 silver dollars. The total amount of the customs gold convertible note reserve fund is 400,9630.07 silver dollars. This reserve fund includes 7,926.290 ounces of pure gold, with a fixed price of 51.68, equivalent to 400,9630.07 customs gold dollars. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve shall be at least 60%, and the remainder shall be guaranteed by legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. December 28, 1936, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fusun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong."

Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Company Holds Founding Meeting in Shanghai; Board of Directors and Supervisors Re-elected in Further Meeting

Jiangxi Guangda Porcelain Co., Ltd., with a projected capital stock of 1 million yuan, most of which has been raised, held its founding meeting at 4 PM the day before yesterday in the auditorium of the World Society on Foch Road. Eighty-five shareholders attended, including Li Shizeng, Du Chongyuan, Hu Xiyuan, Cai Shengbai, and Wu Yun'chu. Li Shizeng was publicly elected as chairman, and after delivering an opening speech, Du Chongyuan, the founder, reported that the company's preparations had taken over two years, and he apologized for the delay due to personal matters. Fortunately, with the enthusiastic support of various sectors, sufficient capital stock was raised. He was grateful for the shareholders' enthusiastic attendance today. Yang Zhiping then reported on the preparations, stating that the stock payments had been received before the year, but due to financial instability, foreign exchange was purchased and deposited in other ports. Subsequently, the government implemented the legal tender policy, so the foreign exchange was sold and deposited in the Central Trust Bureau of China Bank and other local banks, earning about 70,000 yuan in interest. After deducting 50,000 yuan for dividends and over 16,000 yuan for preparatory expenses, there was still a surplus of over 4,000 yuan, which was never used. For the capital stock factory building, four original kilns and two bisque kilns, as well as material warehouses, totaling 1,100 square meters, were built. The construction, including purchasing materials and hiring workers, cost about 110,000 yuan. Construction began on July 15 of this year and is now two-thirds complete. It is expected to be completed in January next year and production will begin in April. Half of the machinery was purchased first, produced by the China Iron Works in Shanghai, and has already been shipped for installation. If the initial production results are good, the remaining parts will be purchased. The generator is an old 300-horsepower machine purchased from the Jiangwan Power Plant and will be shipped within days. The 100-mu factory site is located at the former Anglican Church site at the East Gate of Jiujiang and the vacant prison land, the latter of which was purchased for 8,000 yuan. The company's articles of association were then approved, and directors and supervisors were elected. However, since the Jiangxi Province representatives, including three directors and one supervisor from the province's official shares, had not yet been appointed, it was requested that the election be postponed. This was unanimously approved, and a meeting will be held after the provincial government appoints them to elect them and report to the Ministry of Industry for formal establishment.

Young Woman and Paramour Accused of Falsely Accusing Indian Constable of Rape; Content Untrue, Incomplete, and Extremely Obscene; Case Still Under Investigation, Continued Hearing Tomorrow

Xu Bao'shi, a 21-year-old young woman from Nanjing residing at No. 1340, Rue Robert, Shanghai West, and her paramour, Xu Jinhui, from Xuzhou, were detained the night before last on suspicion of falsely accusing Indian Constable No. 356 from Santoutou, Xinzha Police Station, of rape. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The Public Works Department filed a public prosecution in accordance with Article 169 of the Criminal Code, charging them with false accusation.

The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, then presented the case, stating that at approximately 9 PM last night, the defendants Xu Bao'shi and Xu Jinhui, accompanied by a Chinese constable from No. 1441, reported to the Xinzha Police Station. According to Xu and others, they resided on Rue Robert. At around 8:30 PM, they went out on foot to buy scarves on Stone Road. Xu Bao'shi suddenly felt an urgent need to relieve herself. As the Huangjiasha Garden area was sparsely populated and

the lights were dim,

she went into an alley to urinate. Unexpectedly, three Indians suddenly dragged her into an empty house at No. 14, where one of the Indians raped her. The police verified the confession and sent Xu Dou'shi to the hospital for examination to confirm the rape, but there was no evidence of rape. Shortly after, she identified Indian Constable No. 356 as the rapist. The police inquired with Indian Constable No. 356, who claimed that at around 8 PM last night, he was on duty at the intersection of Avenue Road and Baibaige Road when Xu Jinhui

solicited business

from him, saying that there was a young and beautiful Chinese woman (referring to Xu Dou'shi) available. The constable replied that he was interested but was on duty at the time and would talk about it after his shift. At 8:30 PM, the Indian constable went off duty and went to No. 14, Huangjiasha Garden with Xu Dou'shi, stating that it would cost 1 yuan per hour. As No. 14 was an empty house, Gatekeeper Indian Constable No. 45 was temporarily residing on the second floor. Midway through, he saw Gatekeeper No. 45 and Indian Constable No. 521

talking

, so Indian Constable No. 356 told No. 45 that he wanted to borrow his bedroom as a temporary "balcony." After receiving permission, they went together. Indian Constable No. 356 then had relations with Xu Dou'shi. After about 20 minutes, the constable gave her five single-cent nickel coins. The police found half a yuan in nickel coins on Xu Jinhui. Later, Indian Constable No. 45 told the police that he had also had

relations

with Xu on a previous occasion, in Room 2 of the Sanyi Inn at No. 103, Shunde Road. The police went to the inn and found a record in the register for Room 2 on the 8th of this month, opened by a "Red Ah San," and the teaboy Liu Qinglian could identify her as having stayed with the constable. In addition, Indian Constables No. 705 and No. 130 also reported to the police that Xu Jinhui had previously solicited them as customers and they had stayed with her in Room 24 of the Zhonghua Xin Inn on Avenue Road. Therefore, according to the

above circumstances,

there was no rape. The two defendants, intending to subject another person to criminal punishment, made a false accusation to the police and should be investigated. Indian Constable No. 356 also stated that he had sexual relations with Xu Bao'shi through Xu Jinhui's introduction, stating at the time that it would cost 1 yuan per hour. He only gave her half a yuan because it was only 20 minutes. He had also had

sexual relations

with her once before in September of this year at No. 14.

When questioned, Xu Dou'shi still claimed that she had urinated in Huangjiasha Garden the night before and was dragged into the upper floor of No. 14 by three Indians, one of whom forced himself on her. Afterwards, they forced half a yuan in nickel coins into her pocket, which she gave to her husband. She denied everything else. News from Pengshoutang Pharmacy. Pengshoutang Pharmacy at Xiaoximen in this city has been in operation for many years with an outstanding reputation. The herbs they use are authentic, and they are careful in selecting goods, which has been praised by all sectors. Considering that the A'jing well in Shandong is silted up, and the water for making gelatin can only be found at Huiquan, the pharmacy established a factory in Wuxi in the winter of the 12th year of the Republic of China (1923), drawing water from Huiquan and using gold shovels and silver pots to brew deer antler gelatin, tiger bone gelatin, tortoise plastron gelatin, and donkey-hide gelatin. The products are excellent and popular far and wide. Retail and wholesale are both developed. Products such as Renshen Zaizao Pills and medicated Pinellia ternata are especially popular. As the winter season for nourishing the body approaches, the pharmacy will offer a 10% discount on the actual price on the first and fifteenth days of each lunar month and the first and fifteenth days of each Gregorian month. There is also a Pengshou Economic Herbal Paste, which is sold at a 40% discount on the aforementioned dates to promote widespread use. However, this is limited to the end of the eleventh lunar month, after which the price will be increased. Those who wish to nourish their bodies should purchase them quickly.

Russian Gang of Thieves Planned to Rob in Songjiang; Had Reconnoitered Routes; Court Questioned Them Once Yesterday

The Central Police Station's Chinese and Western detectives recently arrested seven Russian thieves, including Bao Shafu, and confiscated five pistols, over 180 rounds of ammunition, a car, and forged car licenses, among other items. They were handed over to the First Special District Local Court for investigation, as reported in previous newspapers. Investigators have now determined that the Russians went to Songjiang in April and May of this year with the intention of robbing the branch of the Bank of China and the pawnshop there. Therefore, based on the final paragraph of Article 328 of the Criminal Code (attempted robbery) and Article 187 (illegal possession of military firearms), a public prosecution was initiated. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ma ordered Bao Shafu, Na Baofu, Livenf, Ke Shiduo, Maimikang, Di Ketuo, Paikefu, and the other seven defendants to be brought before the court for questioning. The police lawyer, Ru Bao'yi Feng, stated that the defendants had repeatedly traveled to Songjiang, ostensibly to withdraw remittances from the Bank of China branch there, but in reality, they were taking the opportunity to observe the interior of the bank and the routes of entry and exit in order to plan the robbery. Photographs and other items were presented as evidence. After Judge Feng examined them and questioned each of the defendants individually, he ordered them to be returned to detention and scheduled another hearing.

City General Labor Union Holds Group Wedding for City Workers: Ceremony Fee is Four Yuan, Ceremony Simple and Solemn, Regulations and Participation Instructions Have Been Established

The City General Labor Union, recently through the proposal of Commissioners Zhu Xuefan and Shao Xubai, is holding a new-life group wedding for workers and has drafted regulations and participation instructions. These were passed by the Executive Committee of the Union and entrusted to the Welfare Department to organize. The regulations and participation instructions are recorded below:

Wedding Regulations

Shanghai City Worker's New Life Group Wedding Regulations: (1) This Union, in order to promote thrift and implement the New Life Movement, is holding a new-life group wedding for city workers. (2) Any vocational or industrial worker in this city who wishes to hold a wedding may apply to participate in the group wedding ceremony. (3) It is stipulated that four ceremonies will be held each year, the dates to be determined separately and announced. The Chairman of the Union and two standing committee members will officiate. (4) Each participating couple should pay a ceremony fee of four yuan in national currency. (5) Participants should obtain an application form from the Union's Welfare Department in advance, fill it out according to the form, and register the application. After the application is reviewed and approved, the Union will issue a registration certificate. Participants must present the certificate at the specified time. (7) Those approved to participate must strictly abide by the various regulations of the "Participation Instructions for Workers' New Life Group Wedding," and all times and procedures must be absolutely observed. (7) Marriage certificates will be printed and issued by the Union.

Participation Instructions

Participation Instructions for Workers' New Life Group Wedding: (1) Participants should obtain an application form from the Union's Welfare Department and fill it out in triplicate with a brush pen in regular script, without any alterations, stains, or creases. (2) The bride and groom must provide three 4-inch full-body photos and three 2.5-inch half-body photos each. The 4-inch photos should be affixed to the application form, and the 2.5-inch photos should be submitted separately. (3) The parents or guardians of the applicants and the wedding officiant, if they are the same person, must still sign and stamp separately. (4) Each applicant must personally affix their seal. (5) After the application form is filled out clearly according to the regulations and stamped, the bride and groom must personally come to the Union's Welfare Department to register. (If the bride and groom are under the age of twenty, they must be accompanied by the wedding officiant.) (6) After the Union reviews the above application and deems it qualified, a registration certificate will be issued immediately, and the ceremony fee of four yuan in national currency will be paid at the same time. (7) After being approved to participate by the Union, the wedding officiants of both parties should bring the bride and groom to the Union on the date notified by the Union to affix their seals on the marriage certificate. (8) The groom's formal attire for the wedding is stipulated to be domestic goods, and the Union will arrange for the Sanyou Industrial Society to produce it on their behalf. The price per set should not exceed ten yuan. The bride's formal attire will be made of domestic silk and satin, produced on their behalf by the Union's Meiya Silk Weaving Factory. The price should not exceed twelve yuan, or the Union will rent it on their behalf. (9) The bridal bouquet used by the bride at the wedding will be prepared and issued by the Union. (10) The wedding time is set at 2:00 PM. The wedding party should arrive before 1:30 PM. If they fail to arrive on time, the Union may refuse their participation, and the fees paid will not be refunded. (10)(1) No bridesmaids or dress-holders are allowed at the wedding. (10)(2) At the wedding, only the bride and groom and those with tickets will be allowed into the auditorium to observe the ceremony. (10)(3) The aforementioned tickets will be issued together with the registration certificate when the marriage certificate is stamped, ten tickets per couple.

The Main Culprit in the Attempted Assassination Case, Yuan Youlin, Also Arrested: Tried Together with Accomplices, Yuan Admits to Murder

Yuan Youlin, a well-known gangster who occupies an evil influence in the Xieqiao area of ​​Nanshi, is thirty-four years old, has a large number of followers, and specializes in extortion and blackmail. After investigation by the First Special Court, it was found that they had not committed any crimes in the Public Concession. Only Zhu Wenxiu and Jia Shenggen confessed that they were instructed by Yuan Youlin, who was on the run, in August to attempt to murder detective Zhang Rongsheng in the French Concession, which was unsuccessful. The First Special Court sentenced the two criminals, Zhu and Jia, to three months' imprisonment for possession of a pistol. The rest were innocent. The French police sent detectives to transfer the eight criminals, including Zhu, to be brought to justice. At about 9:00 PM the night before, French police inspector Jiang Futian, detective Xie Guangming, and detectives Dai Rongji and Weng Huanzhang were on official business and passed the intersection of Guangxi Road on Sanma Road in the British Concession when they ran into Yuan Youlin, the main culprit in the failed murder of Zhang Rongsheng. They immediately gave chase and arrested Yuan, taking him back to the French police station. Yesterday, Yuan and the eight criminals, including Zhu, were taken to the Criminal Division 1 of the Second Special Court. Police lawyer Yao Judi requested an extension of the investigation to be tried together with the Shi Gengquan case. After review and report by Judge Sun Pengxian, Yuan Youlin, Zhu Wenxiu, and Jia Shenggen confessed to attempting to murder Zhang Rongsheng, while the others denied involvement. The court ordered the defendants to be returned to custody and rescheduled for trial together with the Shi Gengquan case.

Shanghai Neon Light Manufacturing Industry, Edited by China Credit Information Service, A General Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce, Part 41

I. Introduction

In modern times, commercial competition is becoming increasingly fierce. All sectors of industry and commerce are competing to attract customers with novel advertisements. In recent years, the progress of advertising techniques has been rapid, with constant innovation. The invention of neon lights can be said to be a major development in advertising techniques. Today, almost all major cities in the world have this charming purple-blue installation. This is not only an advertising tool for stores, but also an embellishment for the night scene of the city. The Americans call it "the eyes of the night god," and its moving depth is almost imaginable.

Neon light is called Neon Light in English. It was first invented in the German medical field and was originally called "Violet Light" Vio. It was used for the treatment of diseases and, like sun lamps, was an electrotherapy device for treating diseases. Later, a French person modified it and used it as an advertising tool, because its light was beautiful and eye-catching, and everyone who saw it praised it. However, its patent rights have been sold to the American K. Wm. Cloude, so it is also called Colud Neon Luminous Tubing. Some say that it was invented by the American Cloude, which is probably a patent error. However, the Dutch also claim that it was invented by their own people, and to this day, foreign merchants are not allowed to manufacture and operate it in the Netherlands and its territories. Therefore, there are still different opinions about the inventor, and it is impossible to verify. However, judging from the intention, the former should be more credible.

Neon lights are chemically called "neon" or "ne," and the Chinese translation includes the transliterations "Nian Hong" and "Re Hong," and also "Ne Guang." Currently, the name "neon" is more common.

II. History

The first neon light installation in Shanghai was the Royel fountain pen advertisement at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Sichuan Road, which was around 1928. However, the production at that time was not perfect, and there was often a rustling sound, but the people of Shanghai were all amazed by it! When passing by, they would always look up at it. Later, an Italian gentleman set up a factory in Shanghai to manufacture it, but due to limited financial resources and a small scope, coupled with the high cost and the inability to lower the price, the business was not prosperous and soon disappeared. In 1929, Americans RE. Lunkley and others raised US$200,000 to open Cloude Neon Lights, Fed. aInc. U.S.A., in Shanghai, with the factory located at No. 89 Baker Road. Because its products were excellent, and it was also the time of Shanghai's economic prosperity, larger foreign merchants competed to install them, and neon lights in Shanghai shone brightly. However, not many Chinese people installed them at this time.

Later, some foreigners and Chinese people Wan Houji, Shen Lingfang, etc., initiated the organization of the Xinguang Neon Company. Zhang Hualian, the son of former financial decision-maker Zhang Shouyong, initiated the organization of the Meideng Neon Company. Zhou Jiasheng, Cai Guomin, and Yi Jingfu organized the Ziguang Electrical Advertisement Manufacturing Factory. Shanghai's industry gradually increased. However, because the capital of each factory was relatively small and the scope was not large, there were still limited Chinese merchants in Shanghai who were willing to pay high prices for this advertisement, so development was more difficult. However, at that time, it already showed a prosperous trend. This can be said to be the initial stage of the neon light manufacturing industry in Shanghai.

In the summer of 1930, engineering giants Zhang Huikang, Ren Shigang, Chen Junwu, Luo Qingfan, etc., raised 60,000 yuan to open the Dongfang Nianhong Company, which was initially located next to the Commercial Press on Shishan Road. In addition to manufacturing neon lights, it could also manufacture glass tubes itself. This was the largest Chinese-owned company. Although its capital was still far behind Lian, its business development was enough to compete with Lian. In the same year, the newly opened Huade Bulb Factory, Fulaisheng Bulb Factory, etc., also produced neon lights. Later, Tongming, Great Shanghai, Great East, Datong, Lihua, Guangming, etc., factories were successively opened. At this time, the total number of companies in Shanghai was no less than 40. This can be said to be the prosperous era of the industry. (To be continued)

Vendors Causing Trouble for Police: Police File Lawsuit, Prosecuting Under the Articles of Obstructing Official Business, Police Believe Shooting Was Justifiable Self-Defense

In view of the fact that fruit vendors gather in the Nanjing Road-Shanxi Road area every morning, obstructing traffic, the Laoza Police Station dispatched Chinese Constable No. 290 Wang Shirong to drive them away the morning before. After receiving the order, the constable rushed to the scene and ordered the vendors to move their loads away. All the vendors obeyed and left, except for one fruit vendor, Huang Fugen from Jiangyin, who refused to obey and uttered abusive words, insulting and scolding the constable. The constable planned to take Huang to the police station, but Huang actually

Held the Constable Back

And punched him. At that time, many vendors near the area gathered upon hearing the sound, and all were unfavorable to the constable, punching and kicking him. Huang even picked up a large stone and tried to throw it at the constable's head. Fortunately, Zuo Lai, a rickshaw puller, saw it from the side and stepped forward to snatch the stone. Huang was still unwilling and suddenly rushed to the constable, grabbed the constable's gun belt, and tried to snatch his gun. For self-defense, the constable took out his gun, and because at this time

There Were Too Many People and Hands

Accidentally touched the trigger. Two bullets were fired, hitting Huang's right leg and Li Xisheng You Xiaochuanzi's left leg, a passerby. The gathered vendors, seeing that a disaster had been caused, scattered like birds and beasts. At that time, Constable No. 312 of the Zhonghe Bank guard at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shanxi Road also heard the sound and rushed to the scene to help Constable No. 290 arrest Huang and Chen Fanglin from Ningbo who was at the scene, and sent the injured to Renji Hospital for treatment.

After the Police Station Received the Report

It dispatched Chinese Detective Li Ruiqing to investigate the scene. At that time, Shi Heqing from Ningbo, who lived at No. 226 Tianjin Road, said that he had witnessed the entire situation. The detective brought him to the police station. Constable No. 290 and watchman No. 312 identified Shi as also being a perpetrator at the scene, so Shi was immediately detained as well.

Under Investigation by the Police Station

It was determined that the incident was caused by the violent actions of Huang and others, and that the constable's shooting was justifiable self-defense. Therefore, Huang Fugen, Chen Fanglin, and Shi Heqing were detained and sent to the Criminal Division 2 of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu explained the situation and prosecuted under Articles 135 and 136 of the Criminal Code for

Obstructing Official Business

And stated that Huang Fugen was in the hospital due to injuries and could not attend court, so he requested permission to reschedule the hearing. Subsequently, witness Zuo Lai and watchman No. 312 proved what had happened. When Chen Fanglin and Shi Heqing were questioned, they both denied beating the Chinese constable. After review by Judge Pan Zhenyang, he ordered the hearing to be rescheduled for one week.
